<div id="review_266470907" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/266470907" />
    <a title="Perry Whitford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5485442-perry-whitford"><img alt="Perry Whitford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1306266009p2/5485442.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/266470907?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Perry Whitford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Perry Whitford" href="/user/show/5485442-perry-whitford">Perry Whitford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006483779" href="/book/show/1910888.Lord_Valentine_s_Castle">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">I wouldn't even wish this on a Terry Pratchett fan.</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer266470907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8993796910702348661">Two questions, the answers to which I find unfathomable, dominate my thinking about this terrible book:<br/><br/>1) How can Robert Silverberg, an interesting and occasionally excellent writer of countless science fiction and fantasy novels, sometime prose artist of vivid skill and imagination and creator of memorable, generally avaricious or morally dubious characters, write and publish such a childish, asinine piece of vacuous drivel as this book?<br/><br/>2) How in the name of Bilbo Baggins and Gully Foyle did it</span>
  <span id="freeText8993796910702348661" style="display:none">Two questions, the answers to which I find unfathomable, dominate my thinking about this terrible book:<br /><br />1) How can Robert Silverberg, an interesting and occasionally excellent writer of countless science fiction and fantasy novels, sometime prose artist of vivid skill and imagination and creator of memorable, generally avaricious or morally dubious characters, write and publish such a childish, asinine piece of vacuous drivel as this book?<br /><br />2) How in the name of Bilbo Baggins and Gully Foyle did it win both the Hugo and Locus awards in 1981?<br /><br />There is no doubt that Silverberg's golden period was in the late 1960s and early 1970s when he found the courage to write however he wanted, having probably induced a fair stack of the same drugs Philip K Dick was also dabbling with at that time. <br /><br />But I also know that some of his later stuff was good too as I have read and enjoyed both <i>Tom O'Bedlam</i> and <i>The Face of the Waters</i>, which were both written after this risible tosh, so I can't put this down to an irreversible decline in taste and sense.<br /><br />When you think of all the great books that never won either the Hugo or the Locus - let alone both - the mind boggles with regards what that year's panel were thinking!<br /><br />Reading this book can make you want a place a pox on your own house if, like me, you have that ridiculous, masochistic predilection to finish every book you start. <br /><br />I really need to bin that habit, just like I binned this book (once I had read it all first, of course!). </span>
  <a data-text-id="8993796910702348661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2147948289" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2147948289" />
    <a title="The Captain" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54489623-the-captain"><img alt="The Captain" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459976325p2/54489623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2147948289?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Captain" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Captain" href="/user/show/54489623-the-captain">The Captain</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54489623-the-captain?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2147948289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4075597344139702371">Ahoy there me mateys! A little while back, I was introduced to Robert Silverberg’s work with his novella <a href='https://thecaptainsquartersblog.wordpress.com/2017/09/30/on-the-horizon-the-emperor-and-the-maula-robert-silverberg/' rel='nofollow noopener'>the emperor and the maula.</a>. Like I said then, I had absurdly never heard of him. Now if ye be unaware of the author:<br/><br/>I learned from <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/the-emperor-and-the-maula/' rel='nofollow noopener'>sandy @ fantasyliterature</a> that Mr. Silverberg has written no fewer than “78 sci-fi novels, almost 450 short stories and novellas, around 70 books of nonfiction, and around 185 novels of, um, “adult fiction,” in addition to having edited over 130 anthologies.” Talk</span>
  <span id="freeText4075597344139702371" style="display:none">Ahoy there me mateys! A little while back, I was introduced to Robert Silverberg’s work with his novella <a href="https://thecaptainsquartersblog.wordpress.com/2017/09/30/on-the-horizon-the-emperor-and-the-maula-robert-silverberg/" rel="nofollow noopener">the emperor and the maula.</a>. Like I said then, I had absurdly never heard of him. Now if ye be unaware of the author:<br /><br />I learned from <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/the-emperor-and-the-maula/" rel="nofollow noopener">sandy @ fantasyliterature</a> that Mr. Silverberg has written no fewer than “78 sci-fi novels, almost 450 short stories and novellas, around 70 books of nonfiction, and around 185 novels of, um, “adult fiction,” in addition to having edited over 130 anthologies.” Talk about prolific! He is currently 82 years old. Goodreads says that he has won 5 Hugos and 5 Nebulas. Also he is a 2004 Grand Master from the Science Fiction and Fantasy Writers of America. Sheesh!<br /><br />At the time I reached out to the crew for recommendations of what else to read out of his many, many works. Me matey, <a href="https://calmgrove.wordpress.com/about/" rel="nofollow noopener">calmgrove</a>, said “I’ve really enjoyed his Majippoor novels, all set on a giant planet. The first, “Lord Valentine’s Castle”, is very accessible, but to be honest if you don’t want to read the rest if the loosely linked series you won’t feel too denied!”<br /><br />I liked the idea that it was a series that 1) if I liked it I could read more; and 2) it was a self-contained story. Plus a local library had it for free on audiobook. Decision made!<br /><br />It turned out to be an okay read. I didn’t love it but I am glad I read it. I actually loved the world-building, the characters, and the wonderful set-up. The titular character, Valentine, was extremely fun. When ye start the book, Valentine is entering an enormous city in time for a festival. What ye learn is that Valentine has no memories at all. They start at the moment the reader meets him – on the hill on day of his arrival in the big city. Where did he come from? Why is he there? He doesn’t know what to do with himself so he joins a juggling troupe! Fantastic.<br /><br />There were two major problems for me and unfortunately both are pet peeves. The first was that it is a travelogue. I love that ye get to see new places and people but here each are touched on only briefly. I don’t tend to like books where the characters wander around and nothing really exciting happens. In this book, the focus is on Valentine’s struggle to remember his past and then his reluctance to believe it. That reluctance is me second problem. Valentine waffles and hems and haws about his identity even when it has already been proven to the reader and even other characters in the book.<br /><br />I do not like wishy-washy characters or angst. I did understand why Valentine wouldn’t want to take up his old position. I understood why he might want a choice in his life’s path. Who wouldn’t? But I would have liked, after a brief inter-personal struggle, to have seen him embrace his past and then decide how to tackle his future. Instead, the situation is resolved in almost a laughable way with very little action or suspense. Also there are convenient people who happen to come along and offer help at just the right moment. Sigh.<br /><br />Dreams are also a major part of this book. They have real-world consequences and send messages to the people. There are dream readers and dream rulers. Dreams are tied into the ruling of the government. According to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Majipoor_series" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia</a> “The planet is ruled by an unusual tetrarchy: an adoptive Coronal rules in a highly visible and symbolic manner from his palace atop Castle Mount; the previous Coronal retires to become the Pontifex, the head of the bureaucracy in an underground Labyrinth; the Coronal’s mother becomes the Lady of the Isle of Sleep, promoting the morals of Majipoor by sending dreams to its inhabitants; while a hereditary King of Dreams on the distant continent of Suvrael punishes wrongdoers by visiting them with nightmares.” Again cool concept but I was more than a bit confused how they impacted Valentine’s journey.<br /><br />I did happen to love Lisamon Hultin, a giant warrior woman mercenary. She was so fun! And there was an excellent part dealing with the sea and sea serpents. I, of course, adored that section. And truly, I was rooting for Valentine the whole time. While the plot didn’t excite me, I was glad to have this introduction to Majipoor world. I am not adverse to readin’ the second book as it seems to be a collection of individual stories set in a larger framework. Arrr!<br /><br />Check out <a href="https://www.tor.com/2008/12/05/sciencefantasy/" rel="nofollow noopener">this interesting article</a> on the Tor.com website about the novel.<br /><br />Also check out me other reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://thecaptainsquartersblog.wordpress.com/">https://thecaptainsquartersblog.wordp...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4075597344139702371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_468714407" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/468714407" />
    <a title="Kerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/382536-kerry"><img alt="Kerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241083653p2/382536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/468714407?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kerry" href="/user/show/382536-kerry">Kerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16096633-lord-valentine-s-castle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=9">9</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=2007">2007</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer468714407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12489283411331552828">REREAD #1: 9/10 (26 October 2007 - 2 November 2007)<br/><br/><em>Lord Valentine's Castle</em> by Robert Silverberg<br/><br/>Come to the magical planet of Majipoor. Follow Valentine as he joins a motley band of jugglers to seek the secret of his lost past across a wide and wondrous world. In the shattered city of the Shapeshifters, in the temple of the Lady of Sleep and the Isle of the King of Dreams. From the depths of a dying emperor's dark domain, to the destiny that awaits him high atop Lord Valentine's Castle.<br/><br/>I first re</span>
  <span id="freeText12489283411331552828" style="display:none">REREAD #1: 9/10 (26 October 2007 - 2 November 2007)<br /><br /><em>Lord Valentine's Castle</em> by Robert Silverberg<br /><br />Come to the magical planet of Majipoor. Follow Valentine as he joins a motley band of jugglers to seek the secret of his lost past across a wide and wondrous world. In the shattered city of the Shapeshifters, in the temple of the Lady of Sleep and the Isle of the King of Dreams. From the depths of a dying emperor's dark domain, to the destiny that awaits him high atop Lord Valentine's Castle.<br /><br />I first read this book long, long ago. It could easily have been twenty years ago. Then, somewhere in the years of house moves and book culls, my copy vanished. Of course, it was not long afterwards that I found myself with a hankering to reread the book. I checked out second hand copies as well as new, but somehow never quite made the decision to buy - buying books can be a long, complicated and expensive process here in New Zealand, especially if you want one that is older or not particularly popular. In the end, I bought an ecopy from Fictionwise and it then sat on my PDA waiting for me to find the time to read it.<br /><br />I was a little concerned that the book might not stand up to my twenty (or however many) year old memories, but it came up trumps. I greatly enjoyed my long wander through Majipoor with Valentine and the others.<br /><br />The plot is basically simple - the ruler of the world has his throne stolen from him and has to get it back - but Silverberg adds enough twists and turns to make it fresh. Valentine not only loses his throne, but also his memory and even his own body (although, given it was plagued with a limp, he eventually decides he got the better of the deal) and is dumped on the side of the road to make a new life and future. He falls in with a band of jugglers and, finding he has a natural talent for it, becomes one of the troop. However, his new and pleasant simple life is not allowed to last.<br /><br />Plagued by dreams - on a planet where dreams hold truth, secrets and communication - the riddle of his past and identity is eventually revealed. Unable to believe it at first, he still finds himself drawn to follow the clues tossed out to him until he finds this amaing tale is true. From there, he sets about to regain his throne.<br /><br />I like Valentine. At first he is almost simple, untroubled by the weights of life and responsibility, but even as he learns who he is and takes more and more onto himself, that sunny attitude almost never fades completely. The story is told in a close third person POV with Valentine as the focal character, so the only head we ever get inside is his. This means we get to know him very well, while the other characters are never as well developed. All the same, the reader (or this reader anyway) can develop a great liking for them. Besides Valentine himself, Carabella is probably my favourite character and while I fell I know her, I'd still like to know her a little better.<br /><br />But really, it is Majipoor itself that is the star of the story. As Valentine and his companions slowly make their way from one side of the world to the other, the reader is taken on a fantastic journey around an amazing planet. Majipoor was originally home to the Metamorphs, a race of shapechangers, but people from Old Earth arrived fourteen thousand years ago and eventually took possession of the planet. A large range of other alien races also live on Majipoor and all are well described and make fascinating, well-rounded characters. There are the remains of the high-tech that came with the original settlers, but Majipoor is now in many ways more a fantasy world rather than a science fiction one. I love this mixture of the two genres and it is part of the attraction of the series for me.<br /><br />As well as the strange races that populate the planet, the geography and flora and fauna are also unique and fascinating, from a mountain so high it's top sits outside the atmosphere and is maintained by ancient weather machines to amazing plants and creatures, Majipoor is a place of wonders and well worth the visit.<br /><br />Oh, and we mustn't forget the Metamorph plot to regain their lost planet.<br /><br />I never read any of the futher books in the series originally, but I am quite interested in doing so this time. The second book, <em>Majipoor Chronicles</em>, is now sitting on my PDA, waiting for me to have the time to read it.<br /><br /><em>Lord Valentine's Castle</em><br />Majipoor, Book 1<br />Robert Silverberg<br />9/10<br /><br />[Copied across from Library Thing; 3 December 2012]<br /><br /><br />REREAD #2: (3 December 2012 - 15 December 2012)<br /><br />This is still a wonderful book, even on this third (or possibly fourth) reread. I did find it harder than I expected, but I think that's a combination of its length and how busy and tired I've been lately.<br /><br />I find myself to want to stay on Majipoor for a while, so after choosing an in-between book (it ended up being <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13411999.And_All_the_Stars" title="And All the Stars by Andrea K. Höst" rel="nofollow noopener">And All the Stars</a>) I'm now going on with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/252969.Majipoor_Chronicles__Majipoor___2_" title="Majipoor Chronicles (Majipoor, #2) by Robert Silverberg" rel="nofollow noopener">Majipoor Chronicles</a> which I've read once before. I'm hoping this means I'll finally read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/252970.Valentine_Pontifex__Majipoor___3_" title="Valentine Pontifex (Majipoor, #3) by Robert Silverberg" rel="nofollow noopener">Valentine Pontifex</a> at last. I'm also eyes up the other Majipoor books which are currently on sale from SF Gateway in the Amazon.co.uk store. Any courtside cheering towards this goal would be appreciated.<br /><br />P.S. I love the new covers, even if they don’t make much difference to my ebook copies. The big downside to reading this on my Kindle is that I don’t have any decent maps. The images are in the file, but they’re way to small to make anything out. So I borrowed a paper copy from the library so I could check out where everyone was travelling. In a travelogue kind of book, I find it is wonderful to have maps to keep track of where everything is happening. It turns out the re-release edition has new, pretty maps (including a cool sea dragon in the corner of one of them). I’m terribly jealous, but not rich enough to justify double copies. (Although, she muses, they really are very, very <i>nice</i>.) So instead, I’ve requested the new editions of the next two books from the library so I can make use of their maps while I read on the Kindle.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12489283411331552828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_342299358" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/342299358" />
    <a title="Chris Gager" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5295008-chris-gager"><img alt="Chris Gager" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307204529p2/5295008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/342299358?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Gager" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Gager" href="/user/show/5295008-chris-gager">Chris Gager</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060140267" href="/book/show/1836750.Lord_Valentine_s_Castle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer342299358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4897851423134966728">I've been meaning to read this classic ever since I read "Majipoor Chronicles"/"Chronicles of Majipoor" a few years ago. I believe that's the sequel to this book. Will start tonight. Got the book from the Rumford, Me. library via inter-library loan. Read quite a bit on the 80's and 90's; last checked out in 2013.<br/><br/>I suppose it's a bit of overkill for me to be reading two fantasy novels back to back but that's just the way "it"'s turning out. Fate ... This one is sci-fi/fantasy, while "The Crystal </span>
  <span id="freeText4897851423134966728" style="display:none">I've been meaning to read this classic ever since I read "Majipoor Chronicles"/"Chronicles of Majipoor" a few years ago. I believe that's the sequel to this book. Will start tonight. Got the book from the Rumford, Me. library via inter-library loan. Read quite a bit on the 80's and 90's; last checked out in 2013.<br /><br />I suppose it's a bit of overkill for me to be reading two fantasy novels back to back but that's just the way "it"'s turning out. Fate ... This one is sci-fi/fantasy, while "The Crystal Cave" is historical/fantasy. So far its pretty good and typical for the time of it's publication. A tale of far-flung humanity way out in the galaxy somewhere. Plenty of other species around too. Funny that they can all breathe the same atmosphere! Oh well, this IS fantasy, after all. At least I did get a reference to the "why no flying machines" question from the sequel(Majipoor Chronicles), which I read a few years ago. There IS a reason. So, this is a nice page-turner and therefore the only book I've been reading the past couple of days. My time with it is limited because it's an inter-library loan - two weeks ONLY. Other books/series(this is a series) come readily to mind: "The Demon Princes" by Jack Vance is superior, but then the late Mr. Vance was superior to pretty much everybody at this kind of stuff - Smarter and funnier ... "The Lord of the Rings" saga = more intense, more sweeping, just a bit better ... The Crystal Cave = muddier and bloodier and better written ... The "Pern" books by Anne McCaffrey seems very similar ... Harry Potter = also smarter and funnier ... "The Rediscovery of Man" - by Cordwainer Smith and in a class by itself ... Frank Herbert's "Dune" series was the ground-breaker for this kind of stuff ... The "Culture" series = again, brainier and more "au courant." <br /><br />Getting neaer to the end now as Valentine nears the end of his "quest." The author is putting him and his growing entourage through a lot of peril, including TWO aquatic disasters back to back. The second one was a mash-up of Moby-Dick and Jonah and the Whale. One's credulity is being stretched ... Even so, the author's descriptive powers remain top-notch as we get an ever-growing picture of Majipoor. It's quite a place!<br /><br />- Star Wars ... The World of Tiers(Farmer) ... Planet of Adventure(Vance) ... <br /><br />- The verb "flense/flensing" is trotted out. I assume that's a Melville tribute.<br /><br />Getting near the end now and feeling a bit fatigued of it all. A bit boring? ... too drawn out? ... descriptive prose overload? ... could be. Hissune, the star of the next installment, makes his first appearance and livens things up a bit. Seems to me that I liked #2 a bit better than this. RS had the advantage in that one of telling a bunch of disconnected tales from Majipoor's history. It was a short story collection, basically, and the tales were unique in and of themselves, though they all took place on Majipoor. In summation I might conclude that this is a bit dated and wheezy. Still solid all-in-all, but perhaps not as fresh as it might have seemed almost 40 years ago. I'll likely wind up giving it a 3.25*(rounds down to 3*) rating. I think I gave "Majipoor Chronicles" a 3.75*(rounds UP to 4*) rating.<br /><br />Finished last night with this over-long, over-stuffed epic. I needed to engage my skip-skim mode to do it. I must say I finally got tired of Silverberg's faux-Tolkien lingo. The ending twist was kind of neat, and a brief look back by Valentine points to one of the stories in the sequel, one of the "chronicles" of Majipoor from that book. Anyway, I'll stick with my rating from above. A final overview finds that this book, hailed by some as a classic in it's time seems a bit wheezy and stale 40 years on. <br /><br />- Metamorphs = Palestinians<br /><br />- Yuk-yuk - a bit of The Wizard of Oz(the movie) comes in at the end as we find out what/who's behind the curtain.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4897851423134966728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3034842157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3034842157" />
    <a title="prcardi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43250213-prcardi"><img alt="prcardi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471708128p2/43250213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3034842157?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="prcardi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="prcardi" href="/user/show/43250213-prcardi">prcardi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=other-world">other-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=hugo-finalist">hugo-finalist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=rated-r">rated-r</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=exploration">exploration</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3034842157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8633385509742026971">Storyline: 3/5<br/>Characters: 2/5<br/>Writing Style: 3/5<br/>World: 5/5<br/><br/>Normally I would feel confident claiming familiarity with an author after reading eight of his books. With Robert Silverberg having penned more than 200 (and perhaps more than 300) titles, I suppose that it should not be surprising that he showed me something new about himself. I in no way would have recognized this as a Silverberg book. My experience thus far has led me to expect a craftily written short novel with a narrow, promising the</span>
  <span id="freeText8633385509742026971" style="display:none">Storyline: 3/5<br />Characters: 2/5<br />Writing Style: 3/5<br />World: 5/5<br /><br />Normally I would feel confident claiming familiarity with an author after reading eight of his books. With Robert Silverberg having penned more than 200 (and perhaps more than 300) titles, I suppose that it should not be surprising that he showed me something new about himself. I in no way would have recognized this as a Silverberg book. My experience thus far has led me to expect a craftily written short novel with a narrow, promising theme. Silverberg sets up exciting possibilities, tells the tale in the way of one naturally gifted with prose, and ends it with satisfying only the most minimal of expectations. This ninth read was nothing like that. Lord Valentine’s Castle is over 500 pages; has an easy-going, flowery prose that is passively enjoyable; shows no great inspiration; explores no thoughtful idea; and is 100% generic science-fiction/fantasy.<br /><br />The mix of science fiction and fantasy was heavily weighted toward the latter. It was a really good mix, the science fiction simple background adornments, fitting embellishments for the fantasy world. The book aimed for the epic—the long quest with the company of adventurers taking on some heroic struggle. Silverberg also puts together a perfectly enjoyable fantastical world, full of details. The most impressive feature of the fantastical was the world’s scale. I’ll remember that about the book more than anything else. The problem of promising a world with the scale of this one, however, is that it would take a thousand pages or more to adequately immerse oneself in it. This wanting-an-epic-but-unwilling-to-put-in-the-pages problem came to the forefront of my mind several times when reading. We are regularly introduced to new, interesting characters that promise interesting histories or potential maturation. After their introduction they get swept back into the coterie of our main character, largely to be forgotten except as a placeholder among the group. When they do get some moment for the spotlight later in the story, they have admirable competencies and abilities that they’ve never demonstrated before. Presumably that growth should have come in the middle of the novel somewhere, and perhaps it did occur in Silverberg’s head. It never made it to the page, however. Similarly, Silverberg gives us some moments that are supposed to be nostalgically gratifying. The adventures and time elapsed through the book, however, is not sufficient to warrant that sort of looking-back, and it is another reminder that the story could not live up to its epic pretensions. <br /><br />This was a mostly breezy read for its length. The fantasy names were a little overwhelming at the beginning, some of those regularly used not explained until late in the story. This was not of the mysterious reveal variety but merely a I haven’t got around to it yet one. Because there is so much to learn about the world there is a mental investment in books like this. That payoff is higher when there is a sequel that one can easily move onto. Silverberg went on to write nine more books set in this world (two more being direct sequels this one). This book ends the present storyline though it does hint at things the reader might want to come back to explore further. There was nothing so great or remarkable about this story though to make me want to return. With some series I come to actively dislike them and I pettily rejoice when spurning the sequels. I had no dislike for this one – rather it left me with a pleasant warmth. With so much else out there to read, however, any further reading on Majipoor is going to go to the bottom of the reading list. And there’s no guarantee I’ll ever get there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8633385509742026971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2392534455" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2392534455" />
    <a title="Scott Rhee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5717792-scott-rhee"><img alt="Scott Rhee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408223108p2/5717792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2392534455?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott Rhee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott Rhee" href="/user/show/5717792-scott-rhee">Scott Rhee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5717792-scott-rhee?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5717792-scott-rhee?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2392534455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15830508988514550394">Robert Silverberg’s novel “Lord Valentine’s Castle” (first published in 1980) is a clever mix of science fiction and Tolkien-esque fantasy, and I’m pleasantly surprised at how much I enjoyed it. I’m generally not a fan of fantasy as a whole. It’s a genre that I have tried, numerous times, to read and enjoy, but it never quite grabs me in the way that science fiction or even horror grabs me. <br/><br/>While I enjoyed the <i>Fellowship of the Rings</i> series by Tolkien, I have attempted other series with very lit</span>
  <span id="freeText15830508988514550394" style="display:none">Robert Silverberg’s novel “Lord Valentine’s Castle” (first published in 1980) is a clever mix of science fiction and Tolkien-esque fantasy, and I’m pleasantly surprised at how much I enjoyed it. I’m generally not a fan of fantasy as a whole. It’s a genre that I have tried, numerous times, to read and enjoy, but it never quite grabs me in the way that science fiction or even horror grabs me. <br /><br />While I enjoyed the <i>Fellowship of the Rings</i> series by Tolkien, I have attempted other series with very little success. George R.R. Martin’s “Game of Thrones” series was, I thought, very well-written, but I stopped after the second book, not because I didn’t like it but because I felt there were simply too many characters. Plus, most of my favorites were quickly killed off in the second book, so there’s that. I have tried reading Terry Brooks’s <i>Shanarra</i> series but find it to be nothing more than a retread of Tolkein. Terry Goodkind’s “Wizard’s First Rule” put me to sleep, honestly.<br /><br />Ursula LeGuin’s first book in her <i>Earthsea</i> series wowed me, but I have yet to pick up the second book. Stephen King’s <i>Dark Tower</i> series has come the closest to kindling a fiery passion for fantasy in me, as I voraciously read all seven books in that series. Contemporary weird fantasists like Jeff VanderMeer and Neil Gaiman are beginning to win me over with their unique takes on the genre, but I still prefer straight sci-fi and horror.<br /><br />Needless to say, I wasn’t expecting much from Silverberg’s novel. Perhaps the planets were aligned in just the right way, or perhaps the King of Dreams enchanted me with some kind of spell. Whatever the case, I liked it. A lot.<br /><br />The book is set on the planet Majipoor, which has been inhabited by humans for several thousand years, along with other alien species. Travel between the stars is possible but happens infrequently. Majipoor is a planet o’ plenty. <br /><br />The main character is named Valentine, a mysterious figure who has little to no memory of his previous life. It’s as if he awoke one day to find himself a nondescript weary traveler. When he stumbles across a troupe of jugglers, Valentine discovers that he has a talent for the art of juggling.<br /><br />There is something weighing on his mind, however. The thought that he was, perhaps, meant for something more. Even worse, his recurring dreams reveal the possibility that he was once royalty and that he has been brought down by an evil conspiracy.<br /><br />Of course, as it turns out (spoiler alert!), Valentine is truly the rightful heir to the throne of Alhanroel. Somehow, through magical means, his mind has been transferred to the body of a mere farmer, while an imposter takes possession of his body on the royal throne at the top of Castle Mount.<br /><br />Valentine must somehow convince everyone that he is the true Lord Valentine, amass an army to take back his kingdom, and somehow transfer his mind back into his body.<br /><br />Not an easy task, especially for a simple juggler. Than again, maybe a professional juggler is exactly the type of person who can pull it off.<br /><br />Silverberg won me over with a smooth-as-silk prose that evokes Tolkien without sounding lofty and pretentious. There is also a subtle humor to Silverberg, as if he isn’t quite willing to take himself too seriously. (In one scene, Valentine rides into battle in an automobile.) This was my first Silverberg novel, but it won’t be my last.<br /><br />There are, apparently, two more books in the Lord Valentine series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15830508988514550394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_24381949" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24381949" />
    <a title="Mariah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/682776-mariah"><img alt="Mariah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231044317p2/682776.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24381949?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariah" href="/user/show/682776-mariah">Mariah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/682776-mariah?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/682776-mariah?shelf=dan">dan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/682776-mariah?shelf=2008">2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/682776-mariah?shelf=majipoor">majipoor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24381949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18129678224794560025">This book was literally shoved into my hands by my fiance with an exhortation of “You have to read this!” After reading, I have to say, he did me a favor! It takes place on Majipoor, a large planet that was long ago colonized by Earth and races of other planets. Much of the technology has been lost, and Majipoor is at a feudal, agricultural level of development and something of a galactic backwater. But overall, it is a peaceful and prosperous world.<br/><br/>Here we find Valentine, a young man who has fo</span>
  <span id="freeText18129678224794560025" style="display:none">This book was literally shoved into my hands by my fiance with an exhortation of “You have to read this!” After reading, I have to say, he did me a favor! It takes place on Majipoor, a large planet that was long ago colonized by Earth and races of other planets. Much of the technology has been lost, and Majipoor is at a feudal, agricultural level of development and something of a galactic backwater. But overall, it is a peaceful and prosperous world.<br /><br />Here we find Valentine, a young man who has forgotten his past. He joins a troupe of traveling jugglers, and immerses himself in the art and the carefree life of an entertainer. But Valentine is not who he seems, and when he discovers his true identity, he faces a great challenge, and a journey across much of Majipoor.<br /><br />Silverberg has created a fascinating world, filled with many colorful characters of various species. The significance of dreams, and their interpretation, figures prominently in Majipooran culture- even in the social order. The Lady of Sleep guides the people with prophetic dreams, while the King of Dreams punishes wrongdoers with nightmares. It was an exciting and suspenseful adventure. I look forward to the next book in the series, Lord Valentine Pontifex and the continuing political intrigue it will reveal.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18129678224794560025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1605584478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1605584478" />
    <a title="Shawn Thrasher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2148308-shawn-thrasher"><img alt="Shawn Thrasher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549498919p2/2148308.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1605584478?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawn Thrasher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawn Thrasher" href="/user/show/2148308-shawn-thrasher">Shawn Thrasher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781433250620" href="/book/show/7695587-lord-valentine-s-castle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1605584478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5784396777499361090">A feast for the senses as well as the intellect, Silverberg has created a vast world of wonder, part science fiction, part fantasy, part fairy tale, with a just enough of a touch of 1970s sci-fi sexiness. The audio is impeccably narrated by Stefan Rudnicki, whose deep, rich tones are the perfect pairing for a deep, rich novel. Silverberg is a master world builder; you will find few points to quibble on in his gigantic world. What's nice about this series (at least the first three in the series; </span>
  <span id="freeText5784396777499361090" style="display:none">A feast for the senses as well as the intellect, Silverberg has created a vast world of wonder, part science fiction, part fantasy, part fairy tale, with a just enough of a touch of 1970s sci-fi sexiness. The audio is impeccably narrated by Stefan Rudnicki, whose deep, rich tones are the perfect pairing for a deep, rich novel. Silverberg is a master world builder; you will find few points to quibble on in his gigantic world. What's nice about this series (at least the first three in the series; I found his later Majipoor books to be less desirable) is that you can come back to it again and again; it's very re-readable. I'm always surprised this isn't a more beloved series of books. It had been many years, though, since I read this; I found this trip through Majipoor to be as fulfilling as the first time I read it as a teenager. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5784396777499361090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer532447668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer756691746849802143">richly rendered epic fantasy with a scifi twist, which is reminiscent of jack vance. the characters are sympathetic if not compelling, the plot has a flavor of the protag slowly leveling up but still moves quickly enough. a recommended read for fans of the classic SFF epics of the 70s and 80s. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('X2WjxoG3q2Io7AQBkocQOYyUEjkzz5sbjJlDY2Csr3QB23BpqTQmYFS+GJhU2w89B5+Fl/bF6g1LXNdAna2BsQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer14237377776037426087"><i>There are many authors in the database with this name.</i><br/><br/>Robert Silverberg is one of science fiction’s most beloved writers, and the author of such contemporary classics as <i>Dying Inside, Downward to the Earth</i> and <i>Lord Valentine’s Castle,</i> as well as <i>At Winter’s End,</i> also available in a Bison Books edition. He is a past president of the Science Fiction and Fantasy Writers of America and the winner of f</span>
  <span id="freeText14237377776037426087" style="display:none"><i>There are many authors in the database with this name.</i><br /><br />Robert Silverberg is one of science fiction’s most beloved writers, and the author of such contemporary classics as <i>Dying Inside, Downward to the Earth</i> and <i>Lord Valentine’s Castle,</i> as well as <i>At Winter’s End,</i> also available in a Bison Books edition. He is a past president of the Science Fiction and Fantasy Writers of America and the winner of five Nebula Awards and five Hugo Awards. In 2004 the Science Fiction and Fantasy Writers of America presented him with the Grand Master Award. Silverberg is one of twenty-nine writers to have received that distinction. <br /></span>
